        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review of the development of lithium-based rechargeable batteries.  Ongoing research strategies are highlighted, and the challenges that remain regarding the synthesis, characterization, electrochem. performance, and safety of these systems are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGowMxv9DmkLwrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh71yqRvvbrzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3MXovFGitrY%253D&amp;md5=944485672a9bdf09f6e6a7a199bf3d43</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1039/c3nr03594h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fei, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Deng, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Smirnov, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">SBA-15 Confined Synthesis of TiNb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub> Nanoparticles for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">11102</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">11107</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c3nr03594h</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D11102-11107%26journal%3DNanoscale%26author%3DL.%2BFei%26author%3DY.%2BXu%26author%3DX.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DP.%2BXie%26author%3DS.%2BDeng%26author%3DS.%2BSmirnov%26author%3DH.%2BLuo%26title%3DSBA-15%2BConfined%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BTiNb2O7%2BNanoparticles%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc3nr03594h&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b06516&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc3nr03594h&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">SBA-15 confined synthesis of TiNb2O7 nanoparticles for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fei, Ling; Xu, Yun; Wu, Xiaofei; Li, Yuling; Xie, Pu; Deng, Shuguang; Smirnov, Sergei; Luo, Hongmei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11102-11107</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Unlike most conventional anode materials, the newly developed TiNb2O7 (TNO) does not form a solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer, which makes it safe for high power requiring lithium-ion batteries.  In this paper, we demonstrated an SBA-15 confined synthetic approach to prep. TNO nanoparticles (S-TNO) with a small particle size around 10 nm and a large BET surface area of 79.5 m2 g-1.  It is worth mentioning that this is the smallest size reported so far for TNO.  In contrast, the TNO (L-TNO) synthesized without SBA-15 has a particle size above 100 nm and a BET surface area of only 4.3 m2 g-1.  The S-TNO shows better lithium-ion storage properties than L-TNO.  The excellent electrochem. performance of S-TNO is attributed to its small cryst. size, which not only provides a larger effective area for better contact between the electrode material and the electrolyte, but also reduces the rate-limiting Li diffusion path.  Moreover, S-TNO shows a high Coulombic efficiency (above 98% over 300 cycles) and negligible increase of impedance after cycling, which confirms no SEI layer formation in the operational voltage (1-3 V) of TNO.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPhDJA2BnM9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh71yqRvvbrzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhs1OrsLnF&amp;md5=28fd10230e208bd862f240cf08c05827</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1149/06609.0277ecst"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Oxygen-deficient Niobium Oxide in Carbon Matrix as Anode for Lithium-Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ECS Trans.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">66</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">277</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">283</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh71yqRvvbrzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahbi, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A New High-Energy Cathode for a Na-Ion Battery with Ultrahigh Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Young-Uk; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Kwon, Hyung-Soon; Kim, Byoungkook; Kim, Jongsoon; Kim, Haegyeom; Kim, Inkyung; Yoo, Han-Ill; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">135</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13870-13878</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Large-scale elec. energy storage is a key enabler for the use of renewable energy.  Recently, the room-temp. Na-ion battery has been re-highlighted as an alternative low-cost technol. for this application.  However, significant challenges such as energy d. and long-term stability must be addressed.  Herein, we introduce a novel cathode material, Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7, for Na-ion batteries.  This new material provides an energy d. of ∼600 Wh kg-1, the highest value among cathodes, originating from both the multielectron redox reaction (1.2 e- per formula unit) and the high potential (∼3.8 V vs Na+/Na) of the tailored vanadium redox couple (V3.8+/V5+).  Furthermore, an outstanding cycle life (∼95% capacity retention for 100 cycles and ∼84% for extended 500 cycles) could be achieved, which we attribute to the small vol. change (2.9%) upon cycling, the smallest vol. change among known Na intercalation cathodes.  The open crystal framework with two-dimensional Na diffusional pathways leads to low activation barriers for Na diffusion, enabling excellent rate capability.  We believe that this new material can bring the low-cost room-temp.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The first report on excellent cycling stability and superior rate capability of Na3V2(PO4)3 for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Saravanan, Kuppan; Mason, Chad W.; Rudola, Ashish; Wong, Kim Hai; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are attractive for the rapidly emerging large-scale energy storage market for intermittent renewable resources.  Currently a viable cathode material does not exist for practical non-aq. sodium ion battery applications.  Here we disclose a high performance, durable electrode material based on the 3D NASICON framework.  Porous Na3V2(PO4)3/C was synthesized using a novel soln.-based approach.  This material, as a cathode, is capable of delivering an energy storage capacity of ∼400 mWh/g vs. sodium metal.  Furthermore, at high current rates (10, 20 and 40 C), it displayed remarkable capacity retention.  Equally impressive is the long term cycle life.  Nearly 50% of the initial capacity was retained after 30,000 charge/discharge cycles at 40 C (4.7 A/g).  Notably, coulombic efficiency was 99.68% (av.) over the course of cycling.  To the best of our knowledge, the combination of high energy d., high power d. and ultra long cycle life demonstrated here has never been reported before for sodium ion batteries.  We believe our findings will have profound implications for developing large-scale energy storage systems for renewable energy sources.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDJwVCxsh14rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li9IpdR4knKTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXmtFaks7Y%253D&amp;md5=de231bc6c1bc62101fab4472580ebdfa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5358"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Barpanda, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oyama, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nishimura, S.-i.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chung, S.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamada, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A 3.8-V Earth-Abundant Sodium Battery Electrode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable lithium batteries have ushered the wireless revolution over last two decades and are now matured to enable green automobiles. Here we report a hitherto-unknown material with entirely new compn. and structure with the first alluaudite-type sulfate framework, Na2Fe2(SO4)3, registering the highest-ever Fe3+/Fe2+ redox potential at 3.8 V (vs. Na, and hence 4.1 V vs. Li) along with fast rate kinetics.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS2 to Orthorhombic-SnS</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Tengfei; Pang, Wei Kong; Zhang, Chaofeng; Yang, Jianping; Chen, Zhixin; Liu, Hua Kun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8323-8333</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural phase transitions can be used to alter the properties of a material without adding any addnl. elements and are therefore of significant technol. value.  It was found that the hexagonal-SnS2 phase can be transformed into the orthorhombic-SnS phase after an annealing step in an argon atm., and the thus transformed SnS shows enhanced sodium-ion storage performance over that of the SnS2, which is attributed to its structural advantages.  Here, we provide the first report on a SnS@graphene architecture for application as a sodium-ion battery anode, which is built from two-dimensional SnS and graphene nanosheets as complementary building blocks.  The as-prepd. SnS@graphene hybrid nanostructured composite delivers an excellent specific capacity of 940 mAh/g and impressive rate capability of 492 and 308 mAh/g after 250 cycles at the current densities of 810 and 7290 mA/g, resp.  The performance was found to be much better than those of most reported anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  On the basis of combined ex situ Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, XPS, and ex situ X-ray diffraction, the formation mechanism of SnS@graphene and the synergistic Na-storage reactions of SnS in the anode are discussed in detail.  The SnS experienced a two-structural-phase transformation mechanism (orthorhombic-SnS to cubic-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn), while the SnS2 experienced a three-structural-phase transformation mechanism (hexagonal-SnS2 to tetragonal-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn) during the sodiation process.  The lesser structural changes of SnS during the conversion are expected to lead to good structural stability and excellent cycling stability in its sodium-ion battery performance.  These results demonstrate that the SnS@graphene architecture offers unique characteristics suitable for high-performance energy storage application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWHE3xEPCjvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg3ZbyN-XgRRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFChtbbJ&amp;md5=4542b1e918e40b9ce5bae292de5dbcf4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1039/C4NR02044H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ryu, W.-H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, J.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, S.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, I.-D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vine-like MoS<sub>2</sub> Anode Materials Self-Assembled from 1-D Nanofibers for High Capacity Sodium Rechargeable Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">10975</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">10981</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional Tin Disulfide Nanosheets for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Wenping; Rui, Xianhong; Yang, Dan; Sun, Ziqi; Li, Bing; Zhang, Wenyu; Zong, Yun; Madhavi, Srinivasan; Dou, Shixue; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as complementary alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for grid energy storage due to the abundance of sodium.  However, low capacity, poor rate capability, and cycling stability of existing anodes significantly hinder the practical applications of SIBs.  Herein, ultrathin two-dimensional SnS2 nanosheets (3-4 nm in thickness) are synthesized via a facile refluxing process toward enhanced sodium storage.  The SnS2 nanosheets exhibit a high apparent diffusion coeff. of Na+ and fast sodiation/desodiation reaction kinetics.  In half-cells, the nanosheets deliver a high reversible capacity of 733 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, which still remains up to 435 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1.  The cell has a high capacity retention of 647 mA h g-1 during the 50th cycle at 0.1 A g-1, which is by far the best for SnS2, suggesting that nanosheet morphol. is beneficial to improve cycling stability in addn. to rate capability.  The SnS2 nanosheets also show encouraging performance in a full cell with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode.  In addn., the sodium storage mechanism is investigated by ex situ XRD coupled with high-resoln. TEM.  The high specific capacity, good rate capability, and cycling durability suggest that SnS2 nanosheets have great potential working as anodes for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpcqASib5lMkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg3ZbyN-XgRRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1ylt7%252FK&amp;md5=247cb5a5fd9d1ae3d3d725469b1beb50</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/c3cc45254a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Memarzadeh Lotfabad, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Farbod, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kohandehghan, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitlin, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanocrystalline Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub>: a New Anode Material for Rechargeable Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na2Ti3O7 works as an effective low-voltage insertion sodium compd. because of its ability to reversibly uptake 2 Na ions per formula unit (200 mA-h/g) at an av. potential of 0.3 V.  This is the first ever reported oxide to reversibly react with sodium at such a low potential.  Several improvements to the present work are immediately apparent and range from electrode optimization to the detn. of the precise sodium insertion mechanism.  Nevertheless, we believe that the result reported in this paper provides great opportunities in the development of room-temp. high-performing sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8-LOyKHterbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhO1ma1qQNluw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhtV2nt7zO&amp;md5=9d4955e0fada36ace8553399618c3b1b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3478"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guignard, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Didier, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Darriet, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bordet, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Elkaïm, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Delmas, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">P<sub>2</sub>-Na<sub>x</sub>VO<sub>2</sub> System as Electrodes for Batteries and Electron-Correlated Materials</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P2-NaxVO2 system as electrodes for batteries and electron-correlated materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guignard, Marie; Didier, Christophe; Darriet, Jacques; Bordet, Pierre; Elkaim, Erik; Delmas, Claude</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">74-80</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered oxides are the subject of intense studies either for their properties as electrode materials for high-energy batteries or for their original phys. properties due to the strong electronic correlations resulting from their unique structure.  Here the authors present the detailed phase diagram of the layered P2-NaxVO2 system detd. from electrochem. intercalation/deintercalation in Na batteries and in situ x-ray diffraction expts.  Four main single-phase domains exist within the 0.5≤x≤0.9 range.  During the Na deintercalation (intercalation), they differ from one another in the Na/vacancy ordering between the VO2 slabs, which leads to commensurable or incommensurable superstructures.  The electrochem. curve reveals that three peculiar compns. exhibit special structures for x = 1/2, 5/8 and 2/3.  The detailed structural characterization of the P2-Na1/2VO2 phase shows that the Na+ ions are perfectly ordered to minimize Na+/Na+ electrostatic repulsions.  Within the VO2 layers, the V ions form pseudo-trimers with very short V-V distances (two at 2.581 Å and one at 2.687 Å).  This original distribution leads to a peculiar magnetic behavior with a low magnetic susceptibility and an unexpected low Curie const.  This phase also presents a 1st-order structural transition above room temp. accompanied by magnetic and electronic transitions.  This work opens up a new research domain in the field of strongly electron-correlated materials.  From the electrochem. point of view this system may be at the origin of an entire material family optimized by cationic substitutions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGop7YDAopB037Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhO1ma1qQNluw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lattice Breathing Inhibited Layered Vanadium Oxide Ultrathin Nanobelts for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wei, Qiulong; Jiang, Zhouyang; Tan, Shuangshuang; Li, Qidong; Huang, Lei; Yan, Mengyu; Zhou, Liang; An, Qinyou; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18211-18217</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Operating as the "rocking-chair" battery, sodium ion battery (SIB) with acceptable high capacity is a very promising energy storage technol.  Layered vanadium oxide xerogel exhibits high sodium storage capacity.  But it undergoes large lattice breathing during sodiation/desodiation, resulting in fast capacity fading.  Herein, we develop a facile hydrothermal method to synthesize iron preintercalated vanadium oxide ultrathin nanobelts (Fe-VOx) with constricted interlayer spacing.  Using the Fe-VOx as cathode for SIB, the lattice breathing during sodiation/desodiation is largely inhibited and the interlayer spacing is stabilized for reversible and rapid Na+ insertion/extn., displaying enhanced cycling and rate performance.  This work presents a new strategy to reduce the lattice breathing of layered materials for enhanced sodium storage through interlayer spacing engineering.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqMwxAl-KcI3bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhO1ma1qQNluw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlSmtb%252FK&amp;md5=8e10f743407beaa4f90ecb9616f1a287</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.09.019"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bi, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Paranthaman, M.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-organized amorphous TiO2 nanotube arrays on porous Ti foam for rechargeable lithium and sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bi, Zhonghe; Paranthaman, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Self-organized amorphous TiO2 nanotube arrays (NTAs) were successfully fabricated on both Ti foil and porous Ti foam through electrochem. anodization techniques.  The starting Ti foams were fabricated using ARCAM's Electron Beam Melting (EBM) technol.  The TiO2 NTAs on Ti foam were used as anodes in lithium ion batteries; they exhibited high capacities of 103 μAh cm-2 at 10 μA cm-2 and 83 μAh cm-2 at 500 μA cm-2, which are two to three times higher than those achieved on the std. This improvement is mainly attributed to higher surface area of the Ti foam and higher porosity of the nanotube arrays layer grown on the Ti foam.  In addn., a Na-ion half-cell composed of these NTAs anodes and Na metal as the counter electrode showed a self-improved specific capacity upon cycling at 10 μA cm-2.  These results indicate that TiO2 NTAs grown on Ti porous foam are promising electrodes for Li-ion or Na-ion rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQoKGtXutC27Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhO1ma1qQNluw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFSltrzL&amp;md5=3128b3e15618aaf7603602dc09540831</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1021/nl402747x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, K.-T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ali, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chung, K.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anatase Titania Nanorods as an Intercalation Anode Material for Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Ki-Tae; Ali, Ghulam; Chung, Kyung Yoon; Yoon, Chong Seung; Yashiro, Hitoshi; Sun, Yang-Kook; Lu, Jun; Amine, Khalil; Myung, Seung-Taek</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the electrochem. activity of anatase TiO2 nanorods in a Na cell.  The anatase TiO2 nanorods were synthesized by a hydrothermal method, and their surfaces were coated by carbon to improve the elec. cond. by carbonization of pitch at 700° for 2 h in Ar flow.  The resulting structure does not change before and after the carbon coating, as confirmed by x-ray diffraction.  Transmission electron microscopy images confirm the presence of a carbon coating on the anatase TiO2 nanorods.  In cell tests, anodes of bare and carbon-coated anatase TiO2 nanorods exhibit stable cycling performance and attain a capacity of about 172 and 193 mA-h/g on the first charge, resp., in the voltage range of 0-3 V.  With the help of the conductive carbon layers, the carbon-coated anatase TiO2 delivers more capacity at high rates, 104 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g), 82 mA-h/g at the 30C rate (10 A/g), and 53 mA-h/g at the 100C rate (33 A g-1).  By contrast, the anode of bare anatase TiO2 nanorods delivers only about 38 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g).  The excellent cyclability and high-rate capability are the result of a Na+ insertion and extn. reaction into the host structure coupled with Ti4+/3+ redox reaction, as shown by x-ray absorption spectroscopy.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpadjcIpWM-W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhwpCjsqsjQGw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Free-Standing T-Nb2O5/Graphene Composite Papers with Ultrahigh Gravimetric/Volumetric Capacitance for Li-Ion Intercalation Pseudocapacitor</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Lingping; Zhang, Chuanfang; Wang, Jitong; Qiao, Wenming; Ling, Licheng; Long, Donghui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Free-standing electrodes with high gravimetric/volumetric capacitance will open up potential applications in miniaturized consumer electronics.  Herein, we report a simple synthesis technol. of free-standing orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5)/graphene composite papers for Li-intercalating pseudocapacitive electrodes.  Through a facile polyol-mediated solvothermal reaction, the Nb2O5 nanodots are homogeneously decorated onto the surface of reduced graphite oxide (rGO), which can form a homogeneous Nb2O5/rGO colloidal suspension that can be easily fabricated into flexible composite papers.  The heat-treated T-Nb2O5/graphene composite papers exhibit a nanoporous layer-stacked structure with good ionic-elec. conductive pathways, high T-Nb2O5 loading of 74.2%, and high bulk d. of 1.55 g cm-3.  Such T-Nb2O5/graphene composite papers show a superior pseudocapacitor performance as free-standing electrodes, as evidenced by an ultrahigh gravimetric/volumetric capacitance (620.5 F g-1 and 961.8 F cm-3 at 1 mV s-1) and excellent rate capability.  Furthermore, an org. electrolyte-based asym. supercapacitor is assembled based on T-Nb2O5/graphene composite papers, which can deliver a high energy d. of 47 W h kg-1 and power d. of 18 kW kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoOXi8ZK3mEe7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhwpCjsqsjQGw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFyrurrE&amp;md5=96ee3bf0c41cf4902da32bb94797e11e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.matchemphys.2014.10.051"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kong, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Long, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiao, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ling, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrahigh Intercalation Pseudocapacitance of Mesoporous Orthorhombic Niobium Pentoxide from a Novel Cellulose Nanocrystal Template</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Mater.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile biotemplating method was developed to prep. mesoporous orthorhombic nobium pentoxide (T-Nb2O5) films with ultrahigh Li ion (Li+) intercalation pseudocapacitance.  Nanorod-like cellulose nanocrystals (CNs) with 5-10 nm in width and 100-300 nm in length are produced by the hydrolysis of cotton, which can serve as a novel soft templating agent enabling the straightforward synthesis of mesoporous T-Nb2O5 films.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-power and high-energy asymmetric supercapacitors based on Li+-intercalation into orthorhombic Nb2O5/graphene pseudocapacitive electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Lingping; Zhang, Chuanfang; Zhang, Songmin; Wang, Jitong; Cai, Rong; Lv, Chunxiang; Qiao, Wenming; Ling, Licheng; Long, Donghui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intercalation pseudocapacitance which leads to the extraordinary charge storage properties was confirmed as an intrinsic capacitive property of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5) nanocrystals.  However, the poor electronic cond. of T-Nb2O5 nanocrystals may limit their electrochem. use and high-rate performance esp. for thick electrodes with high mass loadings.  To address this issue, the authors herein reported a hydrothermal-heat treatment method to anchor T-Nb2O5 nanocrystals on conductive graphene sheets, which form a layer-by-layer integrated electrode with much shortened ion transport paths and results in excellent electrochem. capacitive properties, including high capacitance (626 C g-1), excellent rate handling and cyclic stability.  Also, asym. supercapacitors were constructed by using the high-rate response T-Nb2O5/graphene nanocomposite and mesoporous C as the neg. and pos. electrode, resp.  The asym. supercapacitor could deliver a high energy d. of 16 W h kg-1 at an unprecedented power d. of 45 kW kg-1 (discharge time of 1.2 s).  The outstanding power properties of the supercapacitors are mainly attributed to the improved high-rate Li-insertion/extn. capability of the T-Nb2O5/graphene electrode and appropriate pairing of the mesoporous C electrode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsk20GPsauJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhwpCjsqsjQGw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsVKnt77N&amp;md5=97691bf44b6adc1548dc8746e3dc9e80</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Augustyn, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Come, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lowe, M.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">518-522</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhwpCjsqsjQGw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1039/C6NR01340F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rui, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zou, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances in Nanostructured Nb-Based Oxides for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8443</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8465</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent advances in nanostructured Nb-based oxides for electrochemical energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Litao; Rui, Xianhong; Chen, Gen; Xu, Weichuan; Zou, Guifu; Luo, Hongmei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8443-8465</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">For the past five years, nanostructured niobium-based oxides have emerged as one of the most prominent materials for batteries, supercapacitors, and fuel cell technologies, for instance, TiNb2O7 as an anode for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), Nb2O5 as an electrode for supercapacitors (SCs), and niobium-based oxides as chem. stable electrochem. supports for fuel cells.  Their high potential window can prevent the formation of lithium dendrites, and their rich redox chem. (Nb5+/Nb4+, Nb4+/Nb3+) makes them very promising electrode materials.  Their unique chem. stability under acid conditions is favorable for practical fuel-cell operation.  In this review, we summarized recent progress made concerning the use of niobium-based oxides as electrodes for batteries (LIBs, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), and vanadium redox flow batteries (VRBs)), SCs, and fuel cell applications.  Moreover, crystal structures, charge storage mechanisms in different crystal structures, and electrochem. performances in terms of the specific capacitance/capacity, rate capability, and cycling stability of niobium-based oxides are discussed.  Insights into the future research and development of niobium-based oxide compds. for next-generation electrochem. devices are also presented.  We believe that this review will be beneficial for research scientists and graduate students who are searching for promising electrode materials for batteries, SCs, and fuel cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo4VUejSd7OabVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFsDW367SjQA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ordered-mesoporous Nb2O5/carbon composite as a sodium insertion material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Lim, Eunho; Jo, Changshin; Yoon, Gabin; Hwang, Jongkook; Jeong, Sanha; Lee, Jinwoo; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The present work introduces a new intercalation host for the Na ions, Nb2O5, and proposes that a mesoporous Nb2O5/carbon composite can function as a promising sodium insertion material.  The highly ordered mesoporous Nb2O5/carbon electrode, synthesized using a block copolymer-assisted one-pot method, demonstrated not only a stable cycle life, but also outstanding rate capability.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile one-step hydrazine-assisted solvothermal synthesis of nitrogen-doped reduced graphene oxide: reduction effect and mechanisms</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Ronghua; Wang, Yan; Xu, Chaohe; Sun, Jing; Gao, Lian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1194-1200</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Homogeneous colloidal dispersions of nitrogen-doped graphene in DMF were readily prepd. through a facile hydrazine-assisted solvothermal redn. method.  The reduced graphene oxide (RGO) sample, prepd. at a wt. ratio of hydrazine to graphene oxide (GO) of 1.4:1 at 180°, was found to possess the highest cond. (2716.2 S m-1) and good dispersibility (0.5 mg mL-1).  This work has not only developed an efficient route to prep. high-quality graphene, but also provides a systematic elucidation of the reaction mechanism for the de-oxygenation of GO based on product characterization.  All of the oxygen-contg. groups were reduced by hydrazine-assisted solvothermal redn.  The deoxygenation of GO and re-establishment of the conjugated graphene network were significantly promoted by hydrazine de-epoxidn., a Wolff-Kishner-Huang-type redn., as well as reactions between metastable NH-NH2 and hydroxyl groups.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced Hybrid Supercapacitor Based on a Mesoporous Niobium Pentoxide/Carbon as High-Performance Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lim, Eunho; Kim, Haegyeom; Jo, Changshin; Chun, Jinyoung; Ku, Kyojin; Kim, Seongseop; Lee, Hyung Ik; Nam, In-Sik; Yoon, Songhun; Kang, Kisuk; Lee, Jinwoo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8968-8978</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, hybrid supercapacitors, which combine the use of battery and supercapacitor, have been extensively studied in order to satisfy increasing demands for high energy d. and high power capability in energy storage devices.  For this purpose, the requirement for anode materials that provide enhanced charge storage sites (high capacity) and accommodate fast charge transport (high rate capability) has increased.  Herein, therefore, a prepn. of nanocomposite as anode material is presented and an advanced hybrid supercapacitor using it is thoroughly analyzed.  The hybrid supercapacitor comprises a mesoporous Nb2O5/carbon (m-Nb2O5-C) nanocomposite anode synthesized by a simple one-pot method using a block copolymer assisted self-assembly and com. activated carbon (MSP-20) cathode under org. electrolyte.  The m-Nb2O5-C anode provides high specific capacity with outstanding rate performance and cyclability, mainly stemming from its enhanced pseudocapacitive behavior through introduction of a carbon-coated mesostructure within a voltage range from 3.0 to 1.1 V (vs. Li/Li+).  The hybrid supercapacitor using the m-Nb2O5-C anode and MSP-20 cathode exhibits excellent energy and power densities (74 W-h/kg and 18,510 W/kg, resp.), with advanced cycle life (capacity retention: ∼90% at 1000 mA/g after 1000 cycles) within potential range 1.0-3.5 V.  In particular, we note that the highest power d. (18,510 W/kg) of hybrid supercapacitor is achieved at 15 W-h/kg, which is the highest level among similar hybrid supercapacitor systems previously reported.  With further study, the hybrid supercapacitors developed in this work could be a next-generation energy storage device, bridging the performance gap between conventional batteries and supercapacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpn4BUf96uJNLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgn-AC9W4i2hQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlynu7zP&amp;md5=c7ea7f4e08a7ba1f0c7067e1162373f7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201306314"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, Y.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered SnS2-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composite - A high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life sodium-ion battery anode material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qu, Baihua; Ma, Chuze; Ji, Ge; Xu, Chaohe; Xu, Jing; Meng, Ying Shirley; Wang, Taihong; Lee, Jim Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High cyclability of carbon-coated TiO2 nanoparticles as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Yeqian; Jiang, Han; Zhu, Jiadeng; Lu, Yao; Chen, Chen; Hu, Yi; Qiu, Yiping; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">157</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">142-148</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to the merits of good chem. stability, elemental abundance and nontoxicity, TiO2 (TiO2) has drawn increasing attraction for use as anode material in Na-ion batteries.  Nanostructured TiO2 was able to achieve high energy d.  However, nanosized TiO2 is typically electrochem. instable, which leads to poor cycling performance.  To improve the cycling stability, C from thermolysis of poly(vinyl pyrrolidone) was coated onto TiO2 nanoparticles.  Electronic cond. and electrochem. stability were enhanced by coating C onto TiO2 nanoparticles.  The resultant C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles exhibited high reversible capacity (242.3 mAh g-1), high coulombic efficiency (97.8%), and good capacity retention (87.0%) at 30 mA g-1 over 100 cycles.  By comparison, untreated TiO2 nanoparticles showed comparable reversible capacity (237.3 mAh g-1) and coulombic efficiency (96.2%), but poor capacity retention (53.2%) under the same condition.  The rate performance of C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles was also displayed ≤127.6 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 800 mA g-1.  The improved cycling performance and rate capability were mostly attributed to protective C layer helping stabilize solid electrolyte interface formation of TiO2 nanoparticles and improving the electronic cond.  Therefore, C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles are promising anode candidate for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcVSv_A0qWyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgn-AC9W4i2hQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlOnurg%253D&amp;md5=845e991863dbb9108adc17af6da9f7f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/am5058037"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.-M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Vogt, B. Interfaces</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">21011</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">21018</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/am5058037</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D21011-21018%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DJ.%2BLee%26author%3DY.-M.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DB.%2BD.%2BVogt%26title%3DFabrication%2Bof%2BPorous%2BCarbon%252FTiO2%2BComposites%2Bthrough%2BPolymerization-Induced%2BPhase%2BSeparation%2Band%2BUse%2Bas%2Ban%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fam5058037&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b06516&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fam5058037&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of Porous Carbon/TiO2 Composites through Polymerization-Induced Phase Separation and Use As an Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Jeongwoo; Chen, Yu-Ming; Zhu, Yu; Vogt, Bryan D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">21011-21018</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Polymn.-induced phase sepn. of nanoparticle-filled soln. is demonstrated as a simple approach to control the structure of porous composites.  These composites are subsequently demonstrated as the active component for sodium-ion battery anode.  To synthesize the composites, we dissolved/dispersed titanium oxide (anatase) nanoparticles (for sodium insertion) and poly(hydroxybutyl methacrylate) (porogen) in furfuryl alc. (carbon precursor) contg. a photoacid generator.  UV exposure converts the photoacid generator to a strong acid that catalyzes the furfuryl alc. polymn.  This polymn. simultaneously decreases the miscibility of the poly(hydroxybutyl methacrylate) and reduces the mobility in the mixt. to kinetically trap the phase sepn.  Carbonization of this polymer composite yields a porous nanocomposite.  This nanocomposite exhibits nearly three-fold greater gravimetric capacity in Na-ion batteries than the same titanium oxide nanoparticles that have been coated with carbon.  This improved performance is attributed to the morphol. as the carbon content in the composite is five times that of the coated nanoparticles.  The porous composite materials exhibit stable cyclic performance.  Moreover, the battery performance using materials from this polymn.-induced phase sepn. method is reproducible (capacity within 10% batch-to-batch).  This simple fabrication methodol. may be extendable to other systems and provides a facile route to generate reproducible hierarchical porous morphol. that can be beneficial in energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp91Lo0orR3MbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgn-AC9W4i2hQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFaqtbvI&amp;md5=2b334e38614a07f0b8d799e370a71752</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.08.051"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">TiO<sub>2</sub>/Carbon Hollow Spheres as Anode Materials for Advanced Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">178</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">871</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">876</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.08.051</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D178%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D871-876%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DF.%2BYang%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BHan%26author%3DK.%2BDu%26author%3DY.%2BLai%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26title%3DTiO2%252FCarbon%2BHollow%2BSpheres%2Bas%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BAdvanced%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2015.08.051&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b06516&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2015.08.051&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiO2/carbon hollow spheres as anode materials for advanced sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Fuhua; Zhang, Zhian; Han, Yu; Du, Ke; Lai, Yanqing; Li, Jie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">178</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">871-876</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2/C hollow spheres (TiO2/C-HSs) were successfully prepd. using a template method.  During the synthesis procedures, SiO2 spheres were used as template, Ti tert-butoxide and dopamine were used as TiO2 and C precursor, resp.  The TiO2/C-HSs were characterized by XRD, N adsorption-desorption measurements, SEM, TEM, TG (TGA) measurements, and Raman spectra anal.  When used as anode materials for Na-ion batteries, the TiO2/C-HSs anode can deliver a high specific capacity and remarkable rate performance.  The excellent electrochem. performance of TiO2/C-HSs can be ascribed to the hollow sphere structure, the existence of C and the large surface area and porous structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqFmAZKyWAjd7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhqEfat_GJVDw"> &gt;&gt;             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Unlike most conventional anode materials, the newly developed TiNb2O7 (TNO) does not form a solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer, which makes it safe for high power requiring lithium-ion batteries.  In this paper, we demonstrated an SBA-15 confined synthetic approach to prep. TNO nanoparticles (S-TNO) with a small particle size around 10 nm and a large BET surface area of 79.5 m2 g-1.  It is worth mentioning that this is the smallest size reported so far for TNO.  In contrast, the TNO (L-TNO) synthesized without SBA-15 has a particle size above 100 nm and a BET surface area of only 4.3 m2 g-1.  The S-TNO shows better lithium-ion storage properties than L-TNO.  The excellent electrochem. performance of S-TNO is attributed to its small cryst. size, which not only provides a larger effective area for better contact between the electrode material and the electrolyte, but also reduces the rate-limiting Li diffusion path.  Moreover, S-TNO shows a high Coulombic efficiency (above 98% over 300 cycles) and negligible increase of impedance after cycling, which confirms no SEI layer formation in the operational voltage (1-3 V) of TNO.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPhDJA2BnM9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljeqy4mbKlrMw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhs1OrsLnF&amp;md5=28fd10230e208bd862f240cf08c05827</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1149/06609.0277ecst"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Oxygen-deficient Niobium Oxide in Carbon Matrix as Anode for Lithium-Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ECS Trans.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">66</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">277</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">283</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Nb2O5-x resulted from partially reduced stoichiometric Nb2O5.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzwsZ6Hk9GEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahbi, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Large-scale elec. energy storage is a key enabler for the use of renewable energy.  Recently, the room-temp. Na-ion battery has been re-highlighted as an alternative low-cost technol. for this application.  However, significant challenges such as energy d. and long-term stability must be addressed.  Herein, we introduce a novel cathode material, Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7, for Na-ion batteries.  This new material provides an energy d. of ∼600 Wh kg-1, the highest value among cathodes, originating from both the multielectron redox reaction (1.2 e- per formula unit) and the high potential (∼3.8 V vs Na+/Na) of the tailored vanadium redox couple (V3.8+/V5+).  Furthermore, an outstanding cycle life (∼95% capacity retention for 100 cycles and ∼84% for extended 500 cycles) could be achieved, which we attribute to the small vol. change (2.9%) upon cycling, the smallest vol. change among known Na intercalation cathodes.  The open crystal framework with two-dimensional Na diffusional pathways leads to low activation barriers for Na diffusion, enabling excellent rate capability.  We believe that this new material can bring the low-cost room-temp. Na-ion battery a step closer to a sustainable large-scale energy storage system.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpMgFNhDwY4a7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzwsZ6Hk9GEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXht1ymtLjL&amp;md5=dfcdb36e705456054d32760606a6f305</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee44004d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">You, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.-L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, Y.-X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y.-G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Quality Prussian Blue Crystals as Superior Cathode Materials for Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         rightTab-cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The first report on excellent cycling stability and superior rate capability of Na3V2(PO4)3 for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Saravanan, Kuppan; Mason, Chad W.; Rudola, Ashish; Wong, Kim Hai; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are attractive for the rapidly emerging large-scale energy storage market for intermittent renewable resources.  Currently a viable cathode material does not exist for practical non-aq. sodium ion battery applications.  Here we disclose a high performance, durable electrode material based on the 3D NASICON framework.  Porous Na3V2(PO4)3/C was synthesized using a novel soln.-based approach.  This material, as a cathode, is capable of delivering an energy storage capacity of ∼400 mWh/g vs. sodium metal.  Furthermore, at high current rates (10, 20 and 40 C), it displayed remarkable capacity retention.  Equally impressive is the long term cycle life.  Nearly 50% of the initial capacity was retained after 30,000 charge/discharge cycles at 40 C (4.7 A/g).  Notably, coulombic efficiency was 99.68% (av.) over the course of cycling.  To the best of our knowledge, the combination of high energy d., high power d. and ultra long cycle life demonstrated here has never been reported before for sodium ion batteries.  We believe our findings will have profound implications for developing large-scale energy storage systems for renewable energy sources.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDJwVCxsh14rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzwsZ6Hk9GEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXmtFaks7Y%253D&amp;md5=de231bc6c1bc62101fab4472580ebdfa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5358"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Barpanda, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oyama, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nishimura, S.-i.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chung, S.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamada, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A 3.8-V Earth-Abundant Sodium Battery Electrode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable lithium batteries have ushered the wireless revolution over last two decades and are now matured to enable green automobiles.  However, the growing concern on scarcity and large-scale applications of lithium resources have steered effort to realize sustainable sodium-ion batteries, Na and Fe being abundant and low-cost charge carrier and redox center, resp.  However, their performance is limited owing to low operating voltage and sluggish kinetics.  Here we report a hitherto-unknown material with entirely new compn. and structure with the first alluaudite-type sulfate framework, Na2Fe2(SO4)3, registering the highest-ever Fe3+/Fe2+ redox potential at 3.8 V (vs. Na, and hence 4.1 V vs. Li) along with fast rate kinetics.  Rare-metal-free Na-ion rechargeable battery system compatible with the present Li-ion battery is now in realistic scope without sacrificing high energy d. and high power, and paves way for discovery of new earth-abundant sustainable cathodes for large-scale batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_sUr2Jpgw1LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzwsZ6Hk9GEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVShs77L&amp;md5=20951f27b1483820983947a5d84d607f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2012.10.038"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ponrouch, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Goñi, A.
