        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural phase transitions can be used to alter the properties of a material without adding any addnl. elements and are therefore of significant technol. value.  It was found that the hexagonal-SnS2 phase can be transformed into the orthorhombic-SnS phase after an annealing step in an argon atm., and the thus transformed SnS shows enhanced sodium-ion storage performance over that of the SnS2, which is attributed to its structural advantages.  Here, we provide the first report on a SnS@graphene architecture for application as a sodium-ion battery anode, which is built from two-dimensional SnS and graphene nanosheets as complementary building blocks.  The as-prepd. SnS@graphene hybrid nanostructured composite delivers an excellent specific capacity of 940 mAh/g and impressive rate capability of 492 and 308 mAh/g after 250 cycles at the current densities of 810 and 7290 mA/g, resp.  The performance was found to be much better than those of most reported anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  On the basis of combined ex situ Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, XPS, and ex situ X-ray diffraction, the formation mechanism of SnS@graphene and the synergistic Na-storage reactions of SnS in the anode are discussed in detail.  The SnS experienced a two-structural-phase transformation mechanism (orthorhombic-SnS to cubic-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn), while the SnS2 experienced a three-structural-phase transformation mechanism (hexagonal-SnS2 to tetragonal-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn) during the sodiation process.  The lesser structural changes of SnS during the conversion are expected to lead to good structural stability and excellent cycling stability in its sodium-ion battery performance.  These results demonstrate that the SnS@graphene architecture offers unique characteristics suitable for high-performance energy storage application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWHE3xEPCjvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljbGwrC33E1eQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFChtbbJ&amp;md5=4542b1e918e40b9ce5bae292de5dbcf4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1039/C4NR02044H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ryu, W.-H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, J.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, S.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, I.-D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vine-like MoS<sub>2</sub> Anode Materials Self-Assembled from 1-D Nanofibers for High Capacity Sodium Rechargeable Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">10975</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">10981</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as complementary alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for grid energy storage due to the abundance of sodium. The SnS2 nanosheets exhibit a high apparent diffusion coeff. of Na+ and fast sodiation/desodiation reaction kinetics.  In half-cells, the nanosheets deliver a high reversible capacity of 733 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, which still remains up to 435 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na2Ti3O7 works as an effective low-voltage insertion sodium compd. because of its ability to reversibly uptake 2 Na ions per formula unit (200 mA-h/g) at an av. potential of 0.3 V.                         rightTab-cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P2-NaxVO2 system as electrodes for batteries and electron-correlated materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guignard, Marie; Didier, Christophe; Darriet, Jacques; Bordet, Pierre; Elkaim, Erik; Delmas, Claude</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered oxides are the subject of intense studies either for their properties as electrode materials for high-energy batteries or for their original phys. properties due to the strong electronic correlations resulting from their unique structure.  Here the authors present the detailed phase diagram of the layered P2-NaxVO2 system detd. from electrochem. intercalation/deintercalation in Na batteries and in situ x-ray diffraction expts.  Four main single-phase domains exist within the 0.5≤x≤0.9 range.  During the Na deintercalation (intercalation), they differ from one another in the Na/vacancy ordering between the VO2 slabs, which leads to commensurable or incommensurable superstructures.  The electrochem. curve reveals that three peculiar compns. exhibit special structures for x = 1/2, 5/8 and 2/3.  The detailed structural characterization of the P2-Na1/2VO2 phase shows that the Na+ ions are perfectly ordered to minimize Na+/Na+ electrostatic repulsions.  Within the VO2 layers, the V ions form pseudo-trimers with very short V-V distances (two at 2.581 Å and one at 2.687 Å).  This original distribution leads to a peculiar magnetic behavior with a low magnetic susceptibility and an unexpected low Curie const.  This phase also presents a 1st-order structural transition above room temp. accompanied by magnetic and electronic transitions.  This work opens up a new research domain in the field of strongly electron-correlated materials.  From the electrochem. point of view this system may be at the origin of an entire material family optimized by cationic substitutions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGop7YDAopB037Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljbGwrC33E1eQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xhs1CktrrL&amp;md5=81ecc8836c7bce554cb56c84708dafe9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201500716"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Niu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-Ion Batteries: Novel K<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C Bundled Nanowires as Superior Sodium-Ion Battery Electrode with Ultrahigh Cycling Stability</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Operating as the "rocking-chair" battery, sodium ion battery (SIB) with acceptable high capacity is a very promising energy storage technol.  Layered vanadium oxide xerogel exhibits high sodium storage capacity.  But it undergoes large lattice breathing during sodiation/desodiation, resulting in fast capacity fading.  Herein, we develop a facile hydrothermal method to synthesize iron preintercalated vanadium oxide ultrathin nanobelts (Fe-VOx) with constricted interlayer spacing.  Using the Fe-VOx as cathode for SIB, the lattice breathing during sodiation/desodiation is largely inhibited and the interlayer spacing is stabilized for reversible and rapid Na+ insertion/extn., displaying enhanced cycling and rate performance.  This work presents a new strategy to reduce the lattice breathing of layered materials for enhanced sodium storage through interlayer spacing engineering.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqMwxAl-KcI3bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljFPD9vDUUbKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlSmtb%252FK&amp;md5=8e10f743407beaa4f90ecb9616f1a287</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.09.019"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bi, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Paranthaman, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Self-organized amorphous TiO2 nanotube arrays (NTAs) were successfully fabricated on both Ti foil and porous Ti foam through electrochem. anodization techniques.  The starting Ti foams were fabricated using ARCAM's Electron Beam Melting (EBM) technol.  The TiO2 NTAs on Ti foam were used as anodes in lithium ion batteries; they exhibited high capacities of 103 μAh cm-2 at 10 μA cm-2 and 83 μAh cm-2 at 500 μA cm-2, which are two to three times higher than those achieved on the std. Ti foil, which is around 40 μAh cm-2 at 10 μA cm-2 and 24 μAh cm-2 at 500 μA cm-2, resp.  This improvement is mainly attributed to higher surface area of the Ti foam and higher porosity of the nanotube arrays layer grown on the Ti foam.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the electrochem. activity of anatase TiO2 nanorods in a Na cell.  The anatase TiO2 nanorods were synthesized by a hydrothermal method, and their surfaces were coated by carbon to improve the elec. cond. by carbonization of pitch at 700° for 2 h in Ar flow.  The resulting structure does not change before and after the carbon coating, as confirmed by x-ray diffraction.  Transmission electron microscopy images confirm the presence of a carbon coating on the anatase TiO2 nanorods.  In cell tests, anodes of bare and carbon-coated anatase TiO2 nanorods exhibit stable cycling performance and attain a capacity of about 172 and 193 mA-h/g on the first charge, resp., in the voltage range of 0-3 V.  With the help of the conductive carbon layers, the carbon-coated anatase TiO2 delivers more capacity at high rates, 104 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g), 82 mA-h/g at the 30C rate (10 A/g), and 53 mA-h/g at the 100C rate (33 A g-1).  By contrast, the anode of bare anatase TiO2 nanorods delivers only about 38 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g).  The excellent cyclability and high-rate capability are the result of a Na+ insertion and extn. reaction into the host structure coupled with Ti4+/3+ redox reaction, as shown by x-ray absorption spectroscopy.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpadjcIpWM-W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljFPD9vDUUbKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXktlGhsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=4bc3a520e6f654a82cbee3b778eef0e7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b04737"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kong, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiao, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ling, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Long, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Free-Standing T-Nb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>/Graphene Composite Papers with Ultrahigh Gravimetric/Volumetric Capacitance for Li-Ion Intercalation Pseudocapacitor</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">9</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">11200</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">11208</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Free-standing electrodes with high gravimetric/volumetric capacitance will open up potential applications in miniaturized consumer electronics.  Herein, we report a simple synthesis technol. of free-standing orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5)/graphene composite papers for Li-intercalating pseudocapacitive electrodes.  Through a facile polyol-mediated solvothermal reaction, the Nb2O5 nanodots are homogeneously decorated onto the surface of reduced graphite oxide (rGO), which can form a homogeneous Nb2O5/rGO colloidal suspension that can be easily fabricated into flexible composite papers.  The heat-treated T-Nb2O5/graphene composite papers exhibit a nanoporous layer-stacked structure with good ionic-elec. conductive pathways, high T-Nb2O5 loading of 74.2%, and high bulk d. of 1.55 g cm-3.  Such T-Nb2O5/graphene composite papers show a superior pseudocapacitor performance as free-standing electrodes, as evidenced by an ultrahigh gravimetric/volumetric capacitance (620.5 F g-1 and 961.8 F cm-3 at 1 mV s-1) and excellent rate capability.  Furthermore, an org. electrolyte-based asym. supercapacitor is assembled based on T-Nb2O5/graphene composite papers, which can deliver a high energy d. of 47 W h kg-1 and power d. of 18 kW kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoOXi8ZK3mEe7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljFPD9vDUUbKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFyrurrE&amp;md5=96ee3bf0c41cf4902da32bb94797e11e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.matchemphys.2014.10.051"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kong, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Long, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiao, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ling, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrahigh Intercalation Pseudocapacitance of Mesoporous Orthorhombic Niobium Pentoxide from a Novel Cellulose Nanocrystal Template</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Mater.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The intercalation pseudocapacitance which leads to the extraordinary charge storage properties was confirmed as an intrinsic capacitive property of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5) nanocrystals.  However, the poor electronic cond. of T-Nb2O5 nanocrystals may limit their electrochem. use and high-rate performance esp. for thick electrodes with high mass loadings.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhHtnG3H6JMLQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1039/C6NR01340F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rui, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zou, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances in Nanostructured Nb-Based Oxides for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8443</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8465</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">For the past five years, nanostructured niobium-based oxides have emerged as one of the most prominent materials for batteries, supercapacitors, and fuel cell technologies, for instance, TiNb2O7 as an anode for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), Nb2O5 as an electrode for supercapacitors (SCs), and niobium-based oxides as chem. stable electrochem. supports for fuel cells.  Their high potential window can prevent the formation of lithium dendrites, and their rich redox chem. (Nb5+/Nb4+, Nb4+/Nb3+) makes them very promising electrode materials.  Their unique chem. stability under acid conditions is favorable for practical fuel-cell operation.  In this review, we summarized recent progress made concerning the use of niobium-based oxides as electrodes for batteries (LIBs, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), and vanadium redox flow batteries (VRBs)), SCs, and fuel cell applications.  Moreover, crystal structures, charge storage mechanisms in different crystal structures, and electrochem. performances in terms of the specific capacitance/capacity, rate capability, and cycling stability of niobium-based oxides are discussed.  Insights into the future research and development of niobium-based oxide compds. for next-generation electrochem. devices are also presented.  We believe that this review will be beneficial for research scientists and graduate students who are searching for promising electrode materials for batteries, SCs, and fuel cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo4VUejSd7OabVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhHtnG3H6JMLQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">The present work introduces a new intercalation host for the Na ions, Nb2O5, and proposes that a mesoporous Nb2O5/carbon composite can function as a promising sodium insertion material.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Homogeneous colloidal dispersions of nitrogen-doped graphene in DMF were readily prepd. through a facile hydrazine-assisted solvothermal redn. method.  The reduced graphene oxide (RGO) sample, prepd. at a wt. ratio of hydrazine to graphene oxide (GO) of 1.4:1 at 180°, was found to possess the highest cond. (2716.2 S m-1) and good dispersibility (0.5 mg mL-1).  This work has not only developed an efficient route to prep. high-quality graphene, but also provides a systematic elucidation of the reaction mechanism for the de-oxygenation of GO based on product characterization. The deoxygenation of GO and re-establishment of the conjugated graphene network were significantly promoted by hydrazine de-epoxidn., a Wolff-Kishner-Huang-type redn., as well as reactions between metastable NH-NH2 and hydroxyl groups.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, hybrid supercapacitors, which combine the use of battery and supercapacitor, have been extensively studied in order to satisfy increasing demands for high energy d. and high power capability in energy storage devices.  For this purpose, the requirement for anode materials that provide enhanced charge storage sites (high capacity) and accommodate fast charge transport (high rate capability) has increased.  Herein, therefore, a prepn. of nanocomposite as anode material is presented and an advanced hybrid supercapacitor using it is thoroughly analyzed.  The hybrid supercapacitor comprises a mesoporous Nb2O5/carbon (m-Nb2O5-C) nanocomposite anode synthesized by a simple one-pot method using a block copolymer assisted self-assembly and com. activated carbon (MSP-20) cathode under org. electrolyte.  The m-Nb2O5-C anode provides high specific capacity with outstanding rate performance and cyclability, mainly stemming from its enhanced pseudocapacitive behavior through introduction of a carbon-coated mesostructure within a voltage range from 3.0 to 1.1 V (vs. Li/Li+).  The hybrid supercapacitor using the m-Nb2O5-C anode and MSP-20 cathode exhibits excellent energy and power densities (74 W-h/kg and 18,510 W/kg, resp.), with advanced cycle life (capacity retention: ∼90% at 1000 mA/g after 1000 cycles) within potential range 1.0-3.5 V.  In particular, we note that the highest power d. (18,510 W/kg) of hybrid supercapacitor is achieved at 15 W-h/kg, which is the highest level among similar hybrid supercapacitor systems previously reported.  With further study, the hybrid supercapacitors developed in this work could be a next-generation energy storage device, bridging the performance gap between conventional batteries and supercapacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpn4BUf96uJNLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhInbGAmIIxmg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlynu7zP&amp;md5=c7ea7f4e08a7ba1f0c7067e1162373f7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201306314"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, Y. Nanostructured TiO2 was able to achieve high energy d.  However, nanosized TiO2 is typically electrochem. instable, which leads to poor cycling performance.  To improve the cycling stability, C from thermolysis of poly(vinyl pyrrolidone) was coated onto TiO2 nanoparticles.  Electronic cond. and electrochem. stability were enhanced by coating C onto TiO2 nanoparticles.  The resultant C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles exhibited high reversible capacity (242.3 mAh g-1), high coulombic efficiency (97.8%), and good capacity retention (87.0%) at 30 mA g-1 over 100 cycles.  By comparison, untreated TiO2 nanoparticles showed comparable reversible capacity (237.3 mAh g-1) and coulombic efficiency (96.2%), but poor capacity retention (53.2%) under the same condition.  The rate performance of C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles was also displayed ≤127.6 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 800 mA g-1.  The improved cycling performance and rate capability were mostly attributed to protective C layer helping stabilize solid electrolyte interface formation of TiO2 nanoparticles and improving the electronic cond.  Therefore, C-coated TiO2 nanoparticles are promising anode candidate for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcVSv_A0qWyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhInbGAmIIxmg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlOnurg%253D&amp;md5=845e991863dbb9108adc17af6da9f7f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1021/am5058037"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.-M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Vogt, B. D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fabrication of Porous Carbon/TiO<sub>2</sub> Composites through Polymerization-Induced Phase Separation and Use as an Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">21011</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">21018</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/am5058037</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of Porous Carbon/TiO2 Composites through Polymerization-Induced Phase Separation and Use As an Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Jeongwoo; Chen, Yu-Ming; Zhu, Yu; Vogt, Bryan D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">21011-21018</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Polymn.-induced phase sepn. of nanoparticle-filled soln. is demonstrated as a simple approach to control the structure of porous composites.  These composites are subsequently demonstrated as the active component for sodium-ion battery anode.  To synthesize the composites, we dissolved/dispersed titanium oxide (anatase) nanoparticles (for sodium insertion) and poly(hydroxybutyl methacrylate) (porogen) in furfuryl alc. (carbon precursor) contg. a photoacid generator.  UV exposure converts the photoacid generator to a strong acid that catalyzes the furfuryl alc. polymn.  This polymn. simultaneously decreases the miscibility of the poly(hydroxybutyl methacrylate) and reduces the mobility in the mixt. to kinetically trap the phase sepn.  Carbonization of this polymer composite yields a porous nanocomposite.  This nanocomposite exhibits nearly three-fold greater gravimetric capacity in Na-ion batteries than the same titanium oxide nanoparticles that have been coated with carbon.  This improved performance is attributed to the morphol. as the carbon content in the composite is five times that of the coated nanoparticles.  The porous composite materials exhibit stable cyclic performance.  Moreover, the battery performance using materials from this polymn.-induced phase sepn. method is reproducible (capacity within 10% batch-to-batch).  This simple fabrication methodol. may be extendable to other systems and provides a facile route to generate reproducible hierarchical porous morphol. that can be beneficial in energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp91Lo0orR3MbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhInbGAmIIxmg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFaqtbvI&amp;md5=2b334e38614a07f0b8d799e370a71752</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.08.051"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">TiO<sub>2</sub>/Carbon Hollow Spheres as Anode Materials for Advanced Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">178</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">871</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">876</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.08.051</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiO2/carbon hollow spheres as anode materials for advanced sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Fuhua; Zhang, Zhian; Han, Yu; Du, Ke; Lai, Yanqing; Li, Jie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">178</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">871-876</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2/C hollow spheres (TiO2/C-HSs) were successfully prepd. using a template method.  During the synthesis procedures, SiO2 spheres were used as template, Ti tert-butoxide and dopamine were used as TiO2 and C precursor, resp.  The TiO2/C-HSs were characterized by XRD, N adsorption-desorption measurements, SEM, TEM, TG (TGA) measurements, and Raman spectra anal.  When used as anode materials for Na-ion batteries, the TiO2/C-HSs anode can deliver a high specific capacity and remarkable rate performance.  The excellent electrochem. performance of TiO2/C-HSs can be ascribed to the hollow sphere structure, the existence of C and the large surface area and porous structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqFmAZKyWAjd7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhInbGAmIIxmg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVagtL%252FK&amp;md5=80ae60196ff0572eb7f95618f4d818c8</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i10">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.6b06516" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.6b06516</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">FESEM, TEM, SEM-EDX mapping, nitrogen adsorption and desorption, TGA, FTIR, 3D structural scheme, CV and cycle performance of samples (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b06516/suppl_file/am6b06516_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b06516/suppl_file/am6b06516_si_001.pdf">am6b06516_si_001.pdf (3.85 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	});

		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

<script nonce="90da8c1e1feeb325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8c1e1feeb325-SJC">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>

var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

                    cookie=status;
